<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Eve_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Eve (disambiguation)">Eve (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Eve Jihan Cooper</b> (<span title="Name at birth"><a href="/wiki/Birth_name#Maiden_and_married_names" title="Birth name">née</a></span> <b>Jeffers</b>; born November 10, 1978) is an American rapper, singer, and actress. In 1999, she released her debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Let_There_Be_Eve...Ruff_Ryders%27_First_Lady" title="Let There Be Eve...Ruff Ryders&#39; First Lady">Let There Be Eve...Ruff Ryders' First Lady</a></i>, which reached number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, making her the third female rapper to accomplish this feat, and was <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certifications" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA certifications">certified</a> double platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA). The album produced the hit singles "<a href="/wiki/What_Ya_Want" title="What Ya Want">What Ya Want</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Love_Is_Blind_(Eve_song)" title="Love Is Blind (Eve song)">Love Is Blind</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Gotta_Man" title="Gotta Man">Gotta Man</a>". That same year, she was featured on <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a>' <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>-winning single "<a href="/wiki/You_Got_Me_(The_Roots_song)" title="You Got Me (The Roots song)">You Got Me</a>", as well as <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Hot_Boyz_(song)" title="Hot Boyz (song)">Hot Boyz</a>", the latter of which peaked within the top ten of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.
</p><p>Eve's second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Scorpion_(Eve_album)" title="Scorpion (Eve album)">Scorpion</a></i> (2001), peaked in the top ten of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and was certified platinum by the RIAA. Its single "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Blow_Ya_Mind" title="Let Me Blow Ya Mind">Let Me Blow Ya Mind</a>", which featured <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a>, won her and Stefani the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Melodic_Rap_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Melodic Rap Performance">Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Collaboration</a> and an <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Award</a>, and peaked at number two on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. Her follow-up album, <i><a href="/wiki/Eve-Olution" title="Eve-Olution">Eve-Olution</a></i> (2002), also peaked in the top ten of the <i>Billboard</i> 200, and yielded the single "<a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Lovin%27" title="Gangsta Lovin&#39;">Gangsta Lovin'</a>", which reached number two on the Hot 100. Her other singles from these albums, "<a href="/wiki/Satisfaction_(Eve_song)" title="Satisfaction (Eve song)">Satisfaction</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Love_Is_Blind_(Eve_song)" title="Love Is Blind (Eve song)">Love Is Blind</a>", as well as her 2007 standalone single, "<a href="/wiki/Tambourine_(song)" title="Tambourine (song)">Tambourine</a>", all reached the top 40 of the Hot 100. She was also featured on Gwen Stefani's song "<a href="/wiki/Rich_Girl_(Gwen_Stefani_song)" title="Rich Girl (Gwen Stefani song)">Rich Girl</a>" in 2005, which was certified double platinum by the RIAA and nominated for a Grammy Award. After parting ways with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>, Eve released <i><a href="/wiki/Lip_Lock" title="Lip Lock">Lip Lock</a></i> (2013), her first independent studio album.
</p><p>As an actress, she starred as Terri Jones in the <a href="/wiki/Comedy_drama" title="Comedy drama">comedy drama</a> films <a href="/wiki/Barbershop_(film)" title="Barbershop (film)"><i>Barbershop</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Barbershop_2:_Back_in_Business" title="Barbershop 2: Back in Business">Barbershop 2: Back in Business</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Barbershop:_The_Next_Cut" title="Barbershop: The Next Cut">Barbershop: The Next Cut</a></i>, and played the lead role of Shelley Williams on the <a href="/wiki/UPN" title="UPN">UPN</a> television sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Eve_(2003_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eve (2003 TV series)">Eve</a></i>. Eve also had supporting roles in the <a href="/wiki/Drama_(film_and_television)" title="Drama (film and television)">drama</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Woodsman_(2004_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Woodsman (2004 film)">The Woodsman</a></i> (2004), the comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cookout" title="The Cookout">The Cookout</a></i> (2004) and the horror film <i><a href="/wiki/Animal_(2014_film)" title="Animal (2014 film)">Animal</a></i> (2014). From 2017 to 2020, she was one of the co-hosts of the <a href="/wiki/CBS_Daytime" title="CBS Daytime">CBS Daytime</a> talk show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Talk_(talk_show)" title="The Talk (talk show)">The Talk</a></i>, for which she earned two <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Daytime Emmy Award">Daytime Emmy Award</a> nominations.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eve Jihan Jeffers was born in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, the daughter of Julie Wilcher, a publishing company supervisor and Jerry Jeffers, a chemical plant supervisor.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Eve lived in <a href="/wiki/West_Philadelphia" title="West Philadelphia">West Philadelphia</a> until age 13 when her family moved to the neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Germantown,_Philadelphia" title="Germantown, Philadelphia">Germantown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-score_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-score-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> She graduated from <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_High_School_(Philadelphia)" title="Martin Luther King High School (Philadelphia)">Martin Luther King High School</a> in Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-score_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-score-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the age of 18, she worked as a stripper until rapper <a href="/wiki/Mase" title="Mase">Mase</a> convinced her to stop stripping.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 1999, Eve discussed stripping in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, saying "that was a hustle, too; there's a song about it on my album, 'Heaven Only Knows.' But I don't regret it – I was eighteen and confused, going through personal problems. I did it for about a month, and I was glad I did it. It helped me find Eve, helped me get serious. It was depressing – a lot of those girls have three or four kids. I'd sit there and be like, 'Eve, you don't belong here, this is not your world.<span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>"<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Eve's first musical interest was singing. She sang in many choirs and even formed an all-female singing group (Dope Girl Posse or EDGP) with a manager.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> This group covered songs from <a href="/wiki/En_Vogue" title="En Vogue">En Vogue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Color_Me_Badd" title="Color Me Badd">Color Me Badd</a>. The group's manager suggested that they should start rapping, and Eve stuck with it. After the group split up, Eve began working on a solo career under the name "Eve of Destruction".<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1998.E2.80.932001:_Beginnings.2C_debut_album_and_breakthrough"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998–2001:_Beginnings,_debut_album_and_breakthrough">1998–2001: Beginnings, debut album and breakthrough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1998–2001: Beginnings, debut album and breakthrough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1998, Eve appeared on the <i><a href="/wiki/Bulworth" title="Bulworth">Bulworth</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Bulworth_(soundtrack)" title="Bulworth (soundtrack)">soundtrack</a> as <b>Eve of Destruction</b> while signed to <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s record label <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a>. She appeared on <a href="/wiki/DMX" title="DMX">DMX</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders%27_Anthem" title="Ruff Ryders&#39; Anthem">Ruff Ryders' Anthem</a>" (Remix) from his album <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Dark_and_Hell_Is_Hot" title="It&#39;s Dark and Hell Is Hot">It's Dark and Hell Is Hot</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a>' single "You Got Me" from the band's fourth album <i><a href="/wiki/Things_Fall_Apart_(album)" title="Things Fall Apart (album)">Things Fall Apart</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Eve also provided background vocals on The Roots' song "Ain't Sayin' Nothin' New" from <i>Things Fall Apart</i> and is credited as Eve of Destruction. Eve's first single "<a href="/wiki/What_Y%27all_Want" class="mw-redirect" title="What Y&#39;all Want">What Y'all Want</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Nokio_the_N-Tity" class="mw-redirect" title="Nokio the N-Tity">Nokio the N-Tity</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dru_Hill" title="Dru Hill">Dru Hill</a>, was released in June 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The song peaked at number 29 on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart and at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Rap_Songs" title="Hot Rap Songs">Hot Rap Songs</a> chart. "What Ya'll Want" was included on the compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Ryde_or_Die_Vol._1" title="Ryde or Die Vol. 1">Ryde or Die Vol. 1</a></i> (1999).<sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Her debut album called <i><a href="/wiki/Let_There_Be_Eve...Ruff_Ryders%27_First_Lady" title="Let There Be Eve...Ruff Ryders&#39; First Lady">Let There Be Eve...Ruff Ryders' First Lady</a></i> was released on September 14, 1999, by <a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders_Entertainment" title="Ruff Ryders Entertainment">Ruff Ryders Entertainment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-score_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-score-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> It sold 213,000 copies in the first week. The album has sold over 2 million copies (according to SoundScan) and is certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">Double Platinum</a>. The album features singles such as "<a href="/wiki/Gotta_Man" title="Gotta Man">Gotta Man</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Love_Is_Blind_(Eve_song)" title="Love Is Blind (Eve song)">Love Is Blind</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> "Love Is Blind" was written when she was 16 and based on her 17-year-old best friend's relationship with a 35-year-old abusive man by whom she became pregnant.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> All of the songs on the album were written by Eve herself. Eve became the third female hip-hop artist to have her album peak at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>'s debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Miseducation_of_Lauryn_Hill" title="The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill">The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill</a></i>, being the first to top the chart in 1998 and <a href="/wiki/Foxy_Brown_(rapper)" title="Foxy Brown (rapper)">Foxy Brown</a>'s second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Chyna_Doll_(album)" title="Chyna Doll (album)">Chyna Doll</a></i> achieving the feat earlier in 1999). In November 1999, Eve was featured on <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Hot_Boyz_(song)" title="Hot Boyz (song)">Hot Boyz (Remix)</a>" along with <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Mo" class="mw-redirect" title="Lil Mo">Lil Mo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Q-Tip (rapper)">Q-Tip</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The remix broke the record for most weeks at number-one on the US R&amp;B chart on the issue dated January 15, 2000; as well as spending 18 weeks at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Rap_Singles" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot Rap Singles">Hot Rap Singles</a> from December 4, 1999, to March 25, 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Eve does not like being referred to as a "Pop Princess." 
Her second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Scorpion_(Eve_album)" title="Scorpion (Eve album)">Scorpion</a></i>, was released on March 6, 2001. She appeared on the cover of <a href="/wiki/Jet_(magazine)" title="Jet (magazine)"><i>Jet</i> magazine</a>, which referred to her as the "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Queen of Rap</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The album's first single, "<a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl%3F_(Eve_song)" title="Who&#39;s That Girl? (Eve song)">Who's That Girl</a>" peaked at number 47 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and number six in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> It was also number 97 on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s 100 Greatest Songs of Hip Hop. The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Blow_Ya_Mind" title="Let Me Blow Ya Mind">Let Me Blow Ya Mind</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a> of <a href="/wiki/No_Doubt" title="No Doubt">No Doubt</a>, peaked at number two on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> in 2002 for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap/Sung_Collaboration" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Collaboration">Best Rap/Sung Collaboration</a>, which was a brand new category at the time. The song was listed at number seven on the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Pazz_%26_Jop" title="Pazz &amp; Jop">Pazz &amp; Jop</a> list, a survey of several hundred music critics conducted by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> A remix of "Love Is Blind" featuring singer <a href="/wiki/Faith_Evans" title="Faith Evans">Faith Evans</a> also appeared on the album. In 2001, Eve won the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Award</a> for Best Female Hip-Hop Artist.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In November 2001, she appeared as a contestant on the game show <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Be_a_Millionaire_(American_game_show)" title="Who Wants to Be a Millionaire (American game show)">Who Wants to Be a Millionaire</a></i> and won $32,000 for her charity.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2002.E2.80.932012:_Eve-Olution.2C_collaborations_and_acting_roles"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2002–2012:_Eve-Olution,_collaborations_and_acting_roles">2002–2012: <i>Eve-Olution,</i> collaborations and acting roles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2002–2012: Eve-Olution, collaborations and acting roles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Eve-03-mika.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Eve-03-mika.jpg/220px-Eve-03-mika.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Eve-03-mika.jpg/330px-Eve-03-mika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Eve-03-mika.jpg/440px-Eve-03-mika.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1339" data-file-height="892" /></a><figcaption>Eve in 2003</figcaption></figure><p>
Eve's third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Eve-Olution" title="Eve-Olution">Eve-Olution</a></i>, was released by <a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders_Entertainment" title="Ruff Ryders Entertainment">Ruff Ryders Entertainment</a> on August 27, 2002, and peaked at number six on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>. The album's first single, "<a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Lovin%27" title="Gangsta Lovin&#39;">Gangsta Lovin'</a>", with <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a>, became her second consecutive number-two hit on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, as well as her third consecutive top ten hit in the United Kingdom. The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Satisfaction_(Eve_song)" title="Satisfaction (Eve song)">Satisfaction</a>" was moderately successful in the United States, reaching number 27 and 22 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 100">Hot 100</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart. <i>Eve-Olution</i> has sold over 500,000 copies in the U.S. and was certified gold in sales by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA). In 2002, Eve appeared on the remixed version of <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Butterflies_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Butterflies (Michael Jackson song)">Butterflies</a>". She appeared in the action film <i><a href="/wiki/XXX_(2002_film)" title="XXX (2002 film)">XXX</a></i> (2002) and all three <a href="/wiki/Barbershop_(film_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbershop (film series)">Barbershop films</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Barbershop_(film)" title="Barbershop (film)">Barbershop</a></i>,<i> <a href="/wiki/Barbershop_2:_Back_in_Business" title="Barbershop 2: Back in Business">Barbershop 2: Back in Business</a></i>, and<i> <a href="/wiki/Barbershop:_The_Next_Cut" title="Barbershop: The Next Cut">Barbershop: The Next Cut</a></i>). In 2003, Eve starred as a fashion designer called Shelly Williams in the television <a href="/wiki/Sitcom" title="Sitcom">sitcom</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Eve_(2003_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eve (2003 TV series)">Eve</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The show followed two sets of male and female friends attempting to navigate relationships with the opposite sex.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The show aired for three seasons on <a href="/wiki/UPN" title="UPN">UPN</a> from September 15, 2003, to May 11, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Eve guest starred as Yvette Powell in an episode of <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s crime drama television series <i><a href="/wiki/Third_Watch" title="Third Watch">Third Watch</a></i>. In 2004, she appeared in two films, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Woodsman_(2004_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Woodsman (2004 film)">The Woodsman</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cookout" title="The Cookout">The Cookout</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></p><figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Eve_in_David_Meister_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Eve_in_David_Meister_1.jpg/208px-Eve_in_David_Meister_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="208" height="313" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Eve_in_David_Meister_1.jpg/313px-Eve_in_David_Meister_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Eve_in_David_Meister_1.jpg/417px-Eve_in_David_Meister_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="5184" /></a><figcaption>Eve at <a href="/wiki/The_Heart_Truth" title="The Heart Truth">The Heart Truth</a>'s Red Dress Collection Fashion Show in 2011</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2005, she appeared on <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Rich_Girl_(Gwen_Stefani_song)" title="Rich Girl (Gwen Stefani song)">Rich Girl</a>", which peaked at number seven on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> in March. In the United States, "Rich Girl" was certified gold, and it received a nomination for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap/Sung_Collaboration" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Collaboration">Best Rap/Sung Collaboration</a> at the <a href="/wiki/47th_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="47th Grammy Awards">47th Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The same year, she appeared on the official remix of <a href="/wiki/Amerie" title="Amerie">Amerie</a>'s number one U.S. R&amp;B single, "<a href="/wiki/1_Thing" title="1 Thing">1 Thing</a>". She also appeared on <a href="/wiki/Keyshia_Cole" title="Keyshia Cole">Keyshia Cole</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Never_(Keyshia_Cole_song)" title="Never (Keyshia Cole song)">Never</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Teairra_Mari" class="mw-redirect" title="Teairra Mari">Teairra Mari</a>'s official remix for "<a href="/wiki/No_Daddy" class="mw-redirect" title="No Daddy">No Daddy</a>". In 2007, Eve appeared on <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Rowland" title="Kelly Rowland">Kelly Rowland</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Like_This_(Kelly_Rowland_song)" title="Like This (Kelly Rowland song)">Like This</a>" which reached the top-ten in Ireland and the United Kingdom,  the top-twenty in Australia and New Zealand, as well as number 30 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In July 2007, Eve made a guest appearance on <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a>'s second single "<a href="/wiki/Wake_Up_Call_(Maroon_5_song)" title="Wake Up Call (Maroon 5 song)">Wake Up Call</a>" on Live <i>45th at Night</i>. In late 2008, she performed "Set It On Fire", which became available on the <i><a href="/wiki/Transporter_3" title="Transporter 3">Transporter 3</a> <a href="/wiki/Soundtrack" title="Soundtrack">soundtrack</a></i>. In April 2009, Eve and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Jon" title="Lil Jon">Lil Jon</a> appeared on the song "<a href="/wiki/Patron_Tequila_(song)" title="Patron Tequila (song)">Patron Tequila</a>", the debut single of girl group <a href="/wiki/Paradiso_Girls" title="Paradiso Girls">Paradiso Girls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She played Ophelia Franklin in the British drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Flashbacks_of_a_Fool" title="Flashbacks of a Fool">Flashbacks of a Fool</a></i> (2008). In 2009, she landed a role as Rosa Sparks in the comedy-drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Whip_It_(film)" title="Whip It (film)">Whip It</a></i>, opposite <a href="/wiki/Elliot_Page" title="Elliot Page">Elliot Page</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drew_Barrymore" title="Drew Barrymore">Drew Barrymore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> It received generally positive reviews from critics but did not perform well financially, having made $16.6 million worldwide against its $15 million budget. Also in 2009, she portrayed La-La Buendia in an episode of <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>' crime drama series <i><a href="/wiki/Numbers_(TV_series)" title="Numbers (TV series)">Numbers</a></i> and appeared in two episodes of <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a>'s musical comedy-drama series <a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)"><i>Glee</i></a>, appearing as <a href="/wiki/Grace_Hitchens" class="mw-redirect" title="Grace Hitchens">Grace Hitchens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> She portrayed Latisha in the crime thriller film <i><a href="/wiki/4.3.2.1." title="4.3.2.1.">4.3.2.1.</a></i> (2010) alongside <a href="/wiki/Emma_Roberts" title="Emma Roberts">Emma Roberts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamsin_Egerton" title="Tamsin Egerton">Tamsin Egerton</a>. Eve hosted the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Africa_Music_Awards_2010" title="MTV Africa Music Awards 2010">2010 MTV Africa Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2010, Eve was featured on the official remix of <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>' song "<a href="/wiki/My_Chick_Bad" title="My Chick Bad">My Chick Bad</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Ludacris_&#91;&#91;Ludacris&#93;&#93;_-_My_Chick_Bad_Remix_feat._Diamond,_Trina,_Eve_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ludacris_[[Ludacris]]_-_My_Chick_Bad_Remix_feat._Diamond,_Trina,_Eve-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In November 2010, Eve performed a rap on <a href="/wiki/Australians" title="Australians">Australian</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Guy_Sebastian" title="Guy Sebastian">Guy Sebastian</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl_(Guy_Sebastian_song)" title="Who&#39;s That Girl (Guy Sebastian song)">Who's That Girl</a>", which reached number one on the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Singles Chart</a> and has been certified 4× Platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-ARIA_Single_Accreditations_2011_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_Single_Accreditations_2011-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In December 2010, Eve was featured on <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a>' song "<a href="/wiki/Speechless_(Alicia_Keys_song)" title="Speechless (Alicia Keys song)">Speechless</a>", which charted at number 71 on the US <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart in early 2011. In March 2011, Eve was featured on <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>' song "<a href="/wiki/Everyday_(Coolin%27)" class="mw-redirect" title="Everyday (Coolin&#39;)">Everyday (Coolin')</a>", the first promotional single from his upcoming album <i><a href="/wiki/Haute_Living" title="Haute Living">Haute Living</a></i>. In April 2011, she appeared on <a href="/wiki/Jill_Scott_(singer)" title="Jill Scott (singer)">Jill Scott</a>'s song "Shame" from her album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Light_of_the_Sun" title="The Light of the Sun">The Light of the Sun</a></i>. She also appeared on Russian rapper <a href="/wiki/Timati" title="Timati">Timati</a>'s new single "<a href="/wiki/SWAGG_(Timati_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="SWAGG (Timati album)">Money In Da Bank</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Gartner" title="Wolfgang Gartner">Wolfgang Gartner</a>'s song "Get Em".<sup id="cite_ref-Timati_&#91;&#91;Timati&#93;&#93;feat._Eve_-_Money_in_the_Bank_(official_video)_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timati_[[Timati]]feat._Eve_-_Money_in_the_Bank_(official_video)-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In April 2012, Eve appeared on <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Shaggy_(musician)" title="Shaggy (musician)">Shaggy</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Girls_Just_Wanna_Have_Fun_(Shaggy_song)" title="Girls Just Wanna Have Fun (Shaggy song)">Girls Just Wanna Have Fun</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.932015:_Lip_Lock_and_label_change"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–2015:_Lip_Lock_and_label_change">2013&#8211;2015: <i>Lip Lock</i> and label change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2013–2015: Lip Lock and label change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Eve_rapper_2013.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Eve_rapper_2013.jpg/165px-Eve_rapper_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="165" height="320" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Eve_rapper_2013.jpg/247px-Eve_rapper_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d1/Eve_rapper_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="309" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>Eve performing at the Roxy in 2013</figcaption></figure><p>In 2007, Eve began working on a new album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Lip_Lock" title="Lip Lock">Lip Lock</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_2007_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid_2007-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Five of the album's songs were produced by <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>, including the singles "<a href="/wiki/Tambourine_(song)" title="Tambourine (song)">Tambourine</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Give_It_to_You_(Eve_song)" title="Give It to You (Eve song)">Give It to You</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Sean_Paul" title="Sean Paul">Sean Paul</a>). "Tambourine" debuted at number 73 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart in the week of April 19, 2007. In the United Kingdom, the song debuted at number 38, two weeks before the song's physical release. "Tambourine" peaked at number 18 there and was her fifth consecutive top twenty solo hit in the UK. The song peaked at number 68 on <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s list of the 100 Best Songs of 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and was placed at number 70 on <a href="/wiki/MTV_Networks_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Networks Asia">MTV Asia</a>'s list of Top 100 Hits of 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> produced the song "All Night Long", in which Eve sings rather than raps.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The album ran into a series of delays due to corporate change at the record label and discontent with the lackluster success of the singles.
</p><p>The album was renamed twice from "Here I Am" to "Flirt" to "Lip Lock". After Eve left <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a> and signed with <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lip_Lock" title="Lip Lock">Lip Lock</a></i> was expected to be released in 2011, but it was delayed again. In 2012, Eve decided to release the album as an independent artist, and stated that there will be several buzz singles before the official single release.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>, Eve stated that "one of the biggest things that I wanted to do on this album was make people realize why they fell in love with me in the first place and then take them on a journey to where I am now musically. My ear is different but I think people will recognize me. I think you'll hear that I'm in a happy place. I miss my music. My hunger is different than the first time around".<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On October 9, 2012, Eve released a promotional single titled "<a href="/wiki/She_Bad_Bad" class="mw-redirect" title="She Bad Bad">She Bad Bad</a>" on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In November 2012, Eve released a series of weekly remixes on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> called <i>EVEstlin' Tuesdays</i>, in which she added freestyle rap verses on 2012 hit singles, such as <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Diamonds_(Rihanna_song)" title="Diamonds (Rihanna song)">Diamonds</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_(singer)" title="Miguel (singer)">Miguel</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Adorn_(song)" title="Adorn (song)">Adorn</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album's first official single, "<a href="/wiki/Make_It_Out_This_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Make It Out This Town">Make It Out This Town</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Gabe_Saporta" title="Gabe Saporta">Gabe Saporta</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cobra_Starship" title="Cobra Starship">Cobra Starship</a> was released on February 23, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rap-Up_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap-Up TV">Rap-Up TV</a></i>, Eve confirmed that the second official single would be "Eve" featuring <a href="/wiki/Jamaicans" title="Jamaicans">Jamaican</a> <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> artist Miss Kitty.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The music video for the song was shot in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> in February 2013 and premiered on <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a> on April 29, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On May 14, 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/Lip_Lock" title="Lip Lock">Lip Lock</a></i> was released under her own label From The Rib Music and distributed through <a href="/wiki/RED_Distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="RED Distribution">Sony/RED</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at number 46 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart. The album features collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dawn_Richards" class="mw-redirect" title="Dawn Richards">Dawn Richards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Kelly" title="Claude Kelly">Claude Kelly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pusha_T" title="Pusha T">Pusha T</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chrisette_Michele" title="Chrisette Michele">Chrisette Michele</a>, Nacho, <a href="/wiki/Gabe_Saporta" title="Gabe Saporta">Gabe Saporta</a>, Propaine, <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> She appeared in the post-apocalyptic action comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Bounty_Killer_(film)" title="Bounty Killer (film)">Bounty Killer</a></i> (2013) and the horror thriller film <i><a href="/wiki/Animal_(2014_film)" title="Animal (2014 film)">Animal</a></i> (2014). In 2014, Eve appeared in two episodes of the <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_(TV_channel)" title="Oxygen (TV channel)">Oxygen</a> reality television series <i><a href="/wiki/Sisterhood_of_Hip_Hop" title="Sisterhood of Hip Hop">Sisterhood of Hip Hop</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> She portrayed Amaya in <a href="/wiki/Lifetime_(TV_network)" title="Lifetime (TV network)">Lifetime</a>'s romantic comedy television film <i><a href="/wiki/With_This_Ring_(2015_film)" title="With This Ring (2015 film)">With This Ring</a></i> (2015) alongside <a href="/wiki/Jill_Scott_(singer)" title="Jill Scott (singer)">Jill Scott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regina_Hall" title="Regina Hall">Regina Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2016.E2.80.93present:_Television_projects"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–present:_Television_projects">2016–present: Television projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2016–present: Television projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2016, it was announced that Eve would join <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a> on her <a href="/wiki/This_Is_What_the_Truth_Feels_Like_Tour" title="This Is What the Truth Feels Like Tour">This Is What the Truth Feels Like Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The tour began on July 12, 2016, in <a href="/wiki/Mansfield,_Massachusetts" title="Mansfield, Massachusetts">Mansfield, Massachusetts</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Xfinity_Center_(Mansfield,_Massachusetts)" title="Xfinity Center (Mansfield, Massachusetts)">Xfinity Center</a> and continued throughout North America before concluding on October 16, 2016, in <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">Inglewood, California</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood,_California)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Forum (Inglewood, California)">The Forum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, she hosted <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s annual event <i><a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Honors" title="Hip Hop Honors">Hip Hop Honors</a>,</i> which honors <a href="/wiki/Old-school_hip-hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Old-school hip-hop">old school</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_age_hip_hop" title="Golden age hip hop">golden age hip hop</a> <a href="/wiki/Rappers" class="mw-redirect" title="Rappers">rappers</a> and contributors for their long-term influence and importance in the history of <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop culture">hip hop culture</a>. In 2017, she portrayed Cecile James in two episodes of <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Satire" title="Satire">satirical</a> <a href="/wiki/Comedy-drama" class="mw-redirect" title="Comedy-drama">comedy-drama</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Daytime_Divas" title="Daytime Divas">Daytime Divas</a></i>. On November 14, 2017, Eve became a co-host of the <a href="/wiki/CBS_Daytime" title="CBS Daytime">CBS Daytime</a> talk show, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Talk_(talk_show)" title="The Talk (talk show)">The Talk</a></i>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Aisha_Tyler" title="Aisha Tyler">Aisha Tyler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, she appeared in several television shows, including <i><a href="/wiki/Jane_the_Virgin" title="Jane the Virgin">Jane the Virgin</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(2015_TV_series)" title="Empire (2015 TV series)">Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celebrity_Family_Feud" title="Celebrity Family Feud">Celebrity Family Feud</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Happy_Together_(American_TV_series)" title="Happy Together (American TV series)">Happy Together</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 12, 2019, Eve released her first single in six years titled "Reload", featuring Jamaican dancehall artist <a href="/wiki/Konshens" title="Konshens">Konshens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In November 2019, Eve and <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a> performed "<a href="/wiki/Rich_Girl_(Gwen_Stefani_song)" title="Rich Girl (Gwen Stefani song)">Rich Girl</a>" on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s competition series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(American_TV_series)" title="The Voice (American TV series)">The Voice</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The special performance celebrated Stefani's debut solo album's 15th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Eve hosted the 47th annual <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Daytime Emmy Award">Daytime Emmy Awards</a> with <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Osbourne" title="Sharon Osbourne">Sharon Osbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Underwood" title="Sheryl Underwood">Sheryl Underwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Ann_Inaba" title="Carrie Ann Inaba">Carrie Ann Inaba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marie_Osmond" title="Marie Osmond">Marie Osmond</a> on June 26, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> She received a second <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Entertainment_Talk_Show_Host" title="Daytime Emmy Award for Outstanding Entertainment Talk Show Host">Daytime Emmy Award nomination for Outstanding Entertainment Talk Show Host</a> along with her <i><a href="/wiki/The_Talk_(talk_show)" title="The Talk (talk show)">The Talk</a></i> co-stars in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>  On the November 2, 2020, episode of The Talk, Eve announced that she would be leaving the show at the end of the year due to the impending lockdown restrictions preventing her from returning to the US, and plans to expand her current family.
</p><p>On March 6, 2021, Eve released a 20th anniversary re-release of her album <i>Scorpion</i> with four new remixes.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On June 16, 2021, Eve and <a href="/wiki/Trina" title="Trina">Trina</a> battled in the webcast series <i><a href="/wiki/Verzuz" title="Verzuz">Verzuz</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 8, 2021, it was announced that Eve was to join the cast of <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">American Broadcasting Company</a>'s music series <i><a href="/wiki/Queens_(American_TV_series)" title="Queens (American TV series)">Queens</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Naturi_Naughton" title="Naturi Naughton">Naturi Naughton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In May 2021, it was announced the show was being picked up for a full series,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> followed by the first official trailer, released on May 18, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> On October 1, 2021, the first promo single from <i>Queens</i> (“Nasty Girl")
was released featuring Eve alongside the cast: <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naturi_Naughton" title="Naturi Naughton">Naturi Naughton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nadine_Velazquez" title="Nadine Velazquez">Nadine Velazquez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> A music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Tim_Story" title="Tim Story">Tim Story</a>, was released on the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> This was followed on October 18, 2021, by another rap song from the <i>Queens </i> soundtrack: “The Introduction”, which was co-written by <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Queens_(American_TV_series)" title="Queens (American TV series)">Queens</a></i> debuted on October 19, 2021, and reviews were largely positive; Caroline Framke for Variety praised the quartet's musical offering, calling their raps “sharp and distinct […] making clear their talent as both individuals and a swaggering collective”.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Angie Han for The Hollywood Reporter called the show “Impressive […] lavish […] magic”.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The show was cancelled in early 2022 after one season.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eve has appeared in music videos throughout her career. She has graced the covers of numerous magazines, including <i><a href="/wiki/Essence_(magazine)" title="Essence (magazine)">Essence</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">Teen People</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Allure_(magazine)" title="Allure (magazine)">Allure</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Paper_(magazine)" title="Paper (magazine)">Paper</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Style" title="Philadelphia Style">Philadelphia Style</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Giant_(magazine)" title="Giant (magazine)">Giant</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Blaze_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Blaze (magazine)">Blaze</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Inked_(magazine)" title="Inked (magazine)">Inked</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Ebony_(magazine)" title="Ebony (magazine)">Ebony</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> She has also appeared in television commercials for <a href="/wiki/Sun_Life_Financial" title="Sun Life Financial">Clarica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sprite_(drink)" title="Sprite (drink)">Sprite</a>. Her print ads include <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Hilfiger_(company)" title="Tommy Hilfiger (company)">Tommy Hilfiger</a> and <a href="/wiki/MAC_Cosmetics" title="MAC Cosmetics">MAC Cosmetics</a>' Viva Glam campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003, Eve launched a clothing line titled Fetish which was targeted towards black women.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Fetish was discontinued in September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eve divides her time between London, Los Angeles and New York. She began dating <a href="/wiki/Maximillion_Cooper" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximillion Cooper">Maximillion Cooper</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The couple became engaged on December 25, 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and married on June 14, 2014, in <a href="/wiki/Ibiza" title="Ibiza">Ibiza</a>, Spain. Eve has four stepchildren, all from Cooper's previous marriage to businesswoman Julie Brangstrup.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In October 2021, Eve announced she was expecting her first child with Cooper, due in February.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Eve and Cooper welcomed their first child, a son, on February 1, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concert_tours">Concert tours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Concert tours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Headlining">Headlining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Headlining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Lip Lock Tour (2013)<sup id="cite_ref-Rap-Up_2013_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rap-Up_2013-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Co-headlining_tour">Co-headlining tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Co-headlining tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Ruff Ryders-Cash Money Tour (2000)<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_News_2000_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_News_2000-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>

<li>Ruff Ryders 20th Anniversary Tour (2017)<sup id="cite_ref-Craighead_2017_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Craighead_2017-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_act">Opening act</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eve_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Opening act">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
